  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c69e159e-629f-457b-9e77-13320260bcac'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_343034749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/343034749" />
    <a title="Wanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda"><img alt="Wanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528903039p2/9246169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/343034749?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanda" href="/user/show/9246169-wanda">Wanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345308382" href="/book/show/1281152.The_Golden_Torc">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=reading-project">reading-project</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9246169-wanda?shelf=female-authors">female-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer343034749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6624950347264955667">Lots of nice twists & turns in this second installment of the Saga of the Pliocene Exile. The worm turns, when humans turn out to be nastier and craftier than their Tanu overlords ever imagined. For one thing, humans are willing to fight dirty. It’s reminiscent of the British facing Native Americans, two different codes of conduct ending in unexpected victories for the less-well-armed side of the conflict. Honour means different things to different cultures and May exploits those differences mas</span>
  <span id="freeText6624950347264955667" style="display:none">Lots of nice twists &amp; turns in this second installment of the Saga of the Pliocene Exile. The worm turns, when humans turn out to be nastier and craftier than their Tanu overlords ever imagined. For one thing, humans are willing to fight dirty. It’s reminiscent of the British facing Native Americans, two different codes of conduct ending in unexpected victories for the less-well-armed side of the conflict. Honour means different things to different cultures and May exploits those differences masterfully.<br /><br />I love May’s involvement of geology in this book, and the couple of appearances by plesiosaurs! Despite the fact that we’re pretty sure that those massive marine reptiles didn’t live in the Pliocene, but still, plesiosaurs!<br /><br />We also discover that becoming psychically operant is not for the faint-hearted, there is pain involved and even necessary for that transformation. Just like childbirth, there is pain &amp; struggle, but once the end product is achieved, there is joy. Unknowingly, the Tanu’s torment of certain humans opens the doorway for operancy. <br /><br />Also an interesting revelation: Mercy (the woman who drew the anthropologist Bryan into exile) has been genetically tested and though she came from the future, she is almost full-blooded Tanu. Which begs the question of how that was possible—presumably some hints will be given in later books. <br /> <br />Aiken Drum continues to be a wild card—showing odd moments of compassion, but mostly looking out for number one, this psychopathic human has angered all sides of the conflict now, Tanu, Firvulag and Human. It remains to be seen if all three cultures can agree on his elimination!<br /><br />A lovely balance of male and female roles, which passes the Bechdel test with flying colours. A pleasure to read.<br /><br />Book 177 of my science fiction and fantasy reading project.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6624950347264955667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180533718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180533718" />
    <a title="Terry " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1262683-terry"><img alt="Terry " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316628758p2/1262683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180533718?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terry " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terry " href="/user/show/1262683-terry">Terry </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345308382" href="/book/show/1281152.The_Golden_Torc">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1262683-terry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1262683-terry?shelf=re-reading">re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1262683-terry?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180533718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12605399161171676269">Thus ends the first half of the Saga of Pliocene Exile. It's a good read, but I did find myself less captivated with this volume of the saga and noticed May's colloquial writing style (unfavourably) a bit more in this volume than the last. To be fair she herself has admitted that her primary goal was to write an exciting adventure story, not _War and Peace_, so I won't hold it against her. <br/><br/>The main conflict between the Tanu overlords and the downtrodden humans that has been brewing for years beh</span>
  <span id="freeText12605399161171676269" style="display:none">Thus ends the first half of the Saga of Pliocene Exile. It's a good read, but I did find myself less captivated with this volume of the saga and noticed May's colloquial writing style (unfavourably) a bit more in this volume than the last. To be fair she herself has admitted that her primary goal was to write an exciting adventure story, not _War and Peace_, so I won't hold it against her. <br /><br />The main conflict between the Tanu overlords and the downtrodden humans that has been brewing for years behind the perennial ancestral war of the Tanu and Firvulag is coming to a head. It is not a simple us-vs-them dicotomy, however, given that many humans are more than happy with the state of affairs under the Tanu regime, and not even those who oppose them are all coming from the same place. Thus May weaves together several different strands that are ultimately destined to meet at the crisis point: Madame Guderian, that ultimate author of the current state of Pliocene humanity, has a plan that she hopes will tip the balance away from the Tanu and towards the somewhat more resilient humans upon whom they have unwitingly become dependent, though it's going to be an uphill battle; meanwhile Aiken Drum tries to foment his own coup, though one within the bounds of Tanu law and society, with the aim of nothing less than overlordship of the current regime (his burgeoning metapsychic powers, along with the support of some Tanu heavy-hitters make his possibility of success more than the long-shot it might at first appear); finally we have the enigmatic and unbalanced hatred of Felice Landry whose own growing metapsychic powers may make her more than a match for any that currently exist on Pliocene earth.<br /><br />A lot happens in this volume and the status quo is certainly shaken to its roots by its culmination, though to find out who the ultimate winners are you'll just have to continue on with the last two volumes of the saga. As an added benefit if you continue you'll have the pleasure of meeting Abaddon himself, Marc Remillard, one of May's most intriguing and enjoyable characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12605399161171676269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3081049828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3081049828" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7087508-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443462298p2/7087508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3081049828?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/7087508-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345308382" href="/book/show/1281152.The_Golden_Torc">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3081049828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7558549356063835411">This is second in the series. It follows the other members of the Green group. It was a good continuation of the overall story. We get more information on the Tanu and Firvulag . Part of me wishes there were books on just them, with no pesky human involvement. Humans mess everything up. Not going to say anything regarding the overall story, if you have read this out of order, you must be lost, more lost than our Group Green. I do have to read the next book : <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41337.The_Nonborn_King__Saga_of_the_Pliocene_Exile___3_' title='The Nonborn King (Saga of the Pliocene Exile, #3) by Julian May' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Nonborn King</a> to get to the end of</span>
  <span id="freeText7558549356063835411" style="display:none">This is second in the series. It follows the other members of the Green group. It was a good continuation of the overall story. We get more information on the Tanu and Firvulag . Part of me wishes there were books on just them, with no pesky human involvement. Humans mess everything up. Not going to say anything regarding the overall story, if you have read this out of order, you must be lost, more lost than our Group Green. I do have to read the next book : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41337.The_Nonborn_King__Saga_of_the_Pliocene_Exile___3_" title="The Nonborn King (Saga of the Pliocene Exile, #3) by Julian May" rel="nofollow noopener">The Nonborn King</a> to get to the end of the story, it is by no means done. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7558549356063835411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156965427?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andreas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andreas" href="/user/show/5175491-andreas">Andreas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156965427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16921325435574201446">The scope of this saga spanning eight novels is staggering. A gate is opened to the past, specifically the Pliocene era. But it is a one-way trip. Adventurous souls travel back, and find a world unlike any they could imagine. Epic conflict rages between ancient races, and the future destiny of man is decided. The initial four books make up The Saga of Pliocene Exile.<br/><br/> * The Many-Coloured Land<br/> * The Golden Torc<br/> * The Nonborn King<br/> * The Adversary<br/><br/>These can be read as a standalone series, but who wou</span>
  <span id="freeText16921325435574201446" style="display:none">The scope of this saga spanning eight novels is staggering. A gate is opened to the past, specifically the Pliocene era. But it is a one-way trip. Adventurous souls travel back, and find a world unlike any they could imagine. Epic conflict rages between ancient races, and the future destiny of man is decided. The initial four books make up The Saga of Pliocene Exile.<br /><br /> * The Many-Coloured Land<br /> * The Golden Torc<br /> * The Nonborn King<br /> * The Adversary<br /><br />These can be read as a standalone series, but who would want to stop there?<br /><br />The “bridge” book deals with first contact and the emergence of humans with “supernatural” powers such as telekinesis.<br /><br /> * Intervention. In the US edition this was divided into “Intervention: Surveillance” and “Intervention: Metaconcert”.<br /><br />The Galactic Milieu Trilogy deals with events after humanity has entered the galactic community.<br /><br /> * Jack the Bodiless<br /> * Diamond Mask<br /> * Magnificat<br /><br />What surprised me as I finally finished the whole thing was how May had meticulously planned the entire arc from the very beginning, with elements important to the last novels referenced in the first. This lends the whole series a sense of completion rare in such works. Considering the fact that it took over 12 years to write, the achievement is even more impressive.<br /><br />The characters are amazing, with rich depths and particular quirks that blend in well with the evolving destiny of humankind. The settings, especially in Exiles are fabulous.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the US covers are beyond awful, but don’t be put off by that. Also unfortunately, the books are out of print, but can be easily found second hand.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.books.rosboch.net/?p=236">http://www.books.rosboch.net/?p=236</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16921325435574201446" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1719546875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1719546875" />
    <a title="prcardi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi"><img alt="prcardi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471708128p2/43250213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1719546875?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prcardi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prcardi" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi">prcardi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345308382" href="/book/show/1281152.The_Golden_Torc">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=pg-13">pg-13</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=evolution">evolution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1719546875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7431539791037778982">Storyline: 3/5<br/>Characters: 2/5<br/>Writing Style: 3/5<br/>World: 3/5<br/><br/>I really enjoyed the series first, The Many-Colored Land, and looked with anticipation to reading this one. The Golden Torc dropped many features that I liked and adopted many devices whose absence I had valued. The writing was not as pleasing and selective as it was in the first. The pacing, likewise, carried forward with momentum this time instead of with choice steps. The first one had a unique identity - not just with the mishmash of t</span>
  <span id="freeText7431539791037778982" style="display:none">Storyline: 3/5<br />Characters: 2/5<br />Writing Style: 3/5<br />World: 3/5<br /><br />I really enjoyed the series first, The Many-Colored Land, and looked with anticipation to reading this one. The Golden Torc dropped many features that I liked and adopted many devices whose absence I had valued. The writing was not as pleasing and selective as it was in the first. The pacing, likewise, carried forward with momentum this time instead of with choice steps. The first one had a unique identity - not just with the mishmash of themes, but with its way of building up anticipation and delivering excitement. This was much more of a standard action-adventure. Of course, it remains aloft of the generic sword and sorcery since it employs science fiction tropes to supplement the sword and paranormal powers in lieu of the sorcery. <br /><br />I'm not enamored with sidequels, and I blame much of the lack of originality on the format. Structurally, however, I was pleased that only half this story was a retelling. Oddly, some of best features of the parallel story were neglected here. Those key and anticipated intersections where characters from different storylines confront one another or where the repercussions of one plot influence another were mostly missing. Similarly, climactic scenes and eagerly awaited events were often omitted entirely. The area in which this has the most to offer is an area in which I was least prepared to appreciate. May is convincing and detailed with her knowledge of the ancient northern Mediterranean and its geology and zoology. I suspect there were hidden gems in the descriptions of geography and topography that were lost on me.<br /><br />I still like the series but am less enamored with May than I was after the first reading. I did like that the story came to a satisfactory resolution here. I know that there are more to the series, and I'll read them to see what new problems and adventures are conjured next. I also hope for a return to the form of the first.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7431539791037778982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18484922-dark-draco?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer675883323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3544322835547711776">These are the first books I have read by this author and I absolutely loved it. In the future, a time portal is discovered that can transport people back to the Pliocene era. A lot of people choose this exile rather than continue living as they have, but a surprise awaits them. A race of aliens crash landed on Earth and dominate the era, using humans in their fight between their two factions, the Tanu and the Firvalug. Torcs control the populace and enhance physic power, creating a world of slav</span>
  <span id="freeText3544322835547711776" style="display:none">These are the first books I have read by this author and I absolutely loved it. In the future, a time portal is discovered that can transport people back to the Pliocene era. A lot of people choose this exile rather than continue living as they have, but a surprise awaits them. A race of aliens crash landed on Earth and dominate the era, using humans in their fight between their two factions, the Tanu and the Firvalug. Torcs control the populace and enhance physic power, creating a world of slavery and magic.<br /><br />In the first book, a group of humans are taken by the aliens and begin discover their own limitations and powers. Some side with the Tanu, some with the Firvalug, some fight to be independent. In the second book, the same group are drawn into ever more complicated intrigues and the fight for humanity begins.<br /><br />I loved the style, the plot, the characters. A really enjoyable read. The premise that our racial myths of fairies and trolls descend from primitive memories of these aliens is just great. I can't wait to read the next two books, which are ready and waiting on my bedside table. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1724543745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1724543745" />
    <a title="Christaaay " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5174626-christaaay"><img alt="Christaaay " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601131659p2/5174626.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1724543745?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christaaay " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christaaay " href="/user/show/5174626-christaaay">Christaaay </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition 9780230767614" href="/book/show/19181240-the-golden-torc">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5174626-christaaay?shelf=female-speculative-fiction-authors">female-speculative-fiction-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5174626-christaaay?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5174626-christaaay?shelf=recommended-to-adults">recommended-to-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5174626-christaaay?shelf=recommended-sci-fi">recommended-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1724543745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8904542815550226046">Three races fight for dominance in Pliocene Europe. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>Premise</b>
</i>: Several million years ago, two factions of a dimorphic alien race took shelter on the most compatible planet: earth. <br/><br/>Fast-forward to the 22nd century, where not all humans are happy with the speed of progress and intergalactic relations with various “exotic” races. Several “misfit” humans portal back to Pliocene Europe to escape their own time. Ironically, these time-traveling refugees of the future must now battle aliens for their</span>
  <span id="freeText8904542815550226046" style="display:none">Three races fight for dominance in Pliocene Europe. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Premise</b>
</i>: Several million years ago, two factions of a dimorphic alien race took shelter on the most compatible planet: earth. <br /><br />Fast-forward to the 22nd century, where not all humans are happy with the speed of progress and intergalactic relations with various “exotic” races. Several “misfit” humans portal back to Pliocene Europe to escape their own time. Ironically, these time-traveling refugees of the future must now battle aliens for their very lives in the past, instead of living in peace and harmony with them in their own time. <br /><br />The saga of the human and alien refugees continues in this second book of the Pliocene Exile. <br /><br /><i>Adult science fiction, Published 1982. Book I was nominated for the Nebula award in 1981 and a Hugo Award in 1982. It won the 1982 Locus Award for Best Science Fiction Novel.</i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>What I Liked</b>
</i>: The plot. The plot of <a href="https://christyluisreviews.wordpress.com/2016/07/01/the-many-colored-land-by-julian-may-and-its-awesome-80s-hair-its-eight-freaking-protags/" rel="nofollow noopener">book I</a>, <i>The Many Colored Land</i>, is split between setup for the time warp (from “intergalactic age earth” to “Pliocene earth”) and the events following the warp—a short plot of political rebellion that takes place in the world of the Pliocene itself.<br /><br /><b>But book II is all Pliocene politics, baby, and the power struggles center on racial survival.</b><br /><br />The Tanu, the dominant exotic race due to their strong mental powers, continually battle their rivals and sister-race, the Firvulag, who lack the technology and mental powers of the Tanu.<br /><br />And humans are the slaves.<br /><br />Because the Tanu struggle to procreate due to earth’s radiation levels (unlike the Firvulag, who are far more numerous), they seek humans with strong mental abilities as mates to carry on their bloodlines and rule the Pliocene empire. As a result, humans with strong mental abilities, such as the madcap trickster Aiken Drum (who always keeps things interesting) or the totally boring but insanely powerful Elizabeth are highly sought after as Tanu mates.<br /><br /><b>So, basically the premise rocks. The author pulls it off with style and it’s a lot of fun.</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>What I Didn’t Like</b>
</i>: (1) My lack of connection with the characters was such that whenever they endured some terrible plot twist of fate, my reaction, instead of crying with the characters, was continually, "HAH! Clever twist, author, I gotta hand it to you." It’s not that the characters were <i>bad</i>; not at all. In fact, for a plot- and milieu-driven book, they were quite good. But I really like to connect with my characters, and I had trouble with that in both books I &amp; II. The main reason is, I think, <br /><br />(2) that as with book I, I would have preferred fewer perspectives. I like reading from the perspective of a small cast anyway, but these books aren’t large enough to fully explore their 8+ character arcs.<br /><br />(3) My third complaint is totally subjective and likely connected to my first complaint, above; but it bothers me that love is never a “great power,” in this series. Hatred, madness and power-lust drive the plot, but love (almost) never does. Pliocene lovers (who have <i>no chemistry,</i> btw) tend to find comfort in their love only until they go mad or die. <br /><br /><b>Love is <i>almost never</i> a powerful plot motivation. Mental powers are the main “force,” in this world.</b><br /><br />Which brings me to (4) my fourth and final complaint: I don’t find the speculative element all that...magical. I know, I know, this is sci-fi, not fantasy; but I still like to find myself wishing I could have a go with the superpowers or whatever. I didn't feel that way about the five great “mental guilds” or “metaphysic clans” that make up a large portion of the speculative element, in this series: Farsensors, Creators, Coercers, psychokinetics (PK), and Redactors. <br /><br /><b>The mindspeak is almost nauseating, at times. It sounds like baby talk: </b> <br /><br /><i>“Atleast they no make Aiken dance their tune viceversa if anything. <br />Not toy like Raimobooby.<br />Nor I Sukeylove if you help.”</i><br /><br />I happen to enjoy whimsy more than MIND CRUSHING POWERS! But a different reader might really enjoy the complexity of the mental gymnastics involved. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Overall</b>
</i>: Julian May knows how to tell a good story. This review may have sounded negative, but I’m really just elucidating my own personal reasons for keeping this book at 3.5 stars, despite the incredible thought put into the premise and pageantry. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>Recommended To</b>
</i>: Male readers of fantasy and sci-fi at my library seem to love this series. Any plot- or milieu-driven readers would eat this up. I recommend it to teen and adult readers of sci-fi. It will appeal to some fantasy readers, but more to sci-fi readers, I think.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Book III?</b>
</i>: I think I'll give it a shot. The plot sounds interesting and I like the direction things are going with Aiken Drum...<br /><br /><b>If you liked this review, you can read more of my speculative fiction reviews on my blog, <a href="https://christyluisreviews.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8904542815550226046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_512217222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512217222" />
    <a title="Roddy Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160463-roddy-williams"><img alt="Roddy Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358104537p2/2160463.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512217222?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roddy Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roddy Williams" href="/user/show/2160463-roddy-williams">Roddy Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330267199" href="/book/show/1018534.The_Golden_Torc">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160463-roddy-williams?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160463-roddy-williams?shelf=first-contact">first-contact</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160463-roddy-williams?shelf=time">time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160463-roddy-williams?shelf=psi-powers">psi-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160463-roddy-williams?shelf=saga">saga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2160463-roddy-williams?shelf=human-origins">human-origins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer512217222&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512217222" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7252308113528516253">‘Book Two in the Saga of the Exiles<br/><br/>Exiled beyond the time-portal into a world of six million years before, the misfits of the 22nd century are enmeshed in the age-old war of two alien races.<br/><br/>In this strange world, each year brings the ritual Grand Comabt between the Firvulag and the Tanu, possessors of the invincible mind-armouring necklet…<br/><br/>THE GOLDEN TORC’<br/><br/>Blurb to the 1982 Pan paperback edition<br/><br/>The second episode of The Saga of The Exiles takes us deeper into May’s bizarre, cruel and beautiful Pli</span>
  <span id="freeText7252308113528516253" style="display:none">‘Book Two in the Saga of the Exiles<br /><br />Exiled beyond the time-portal into a world of six million years before, the misfits of the 22nd century are enmeshed in the age-old war of two alien races.<br /><br />In this strange world, each year brings the ritual Grand Comabt between the Firvulag and the Tanu, possessors of the invincible mind-armouring necklet…<br /><br />THE GOLDEN TORC’<br /><br />Blurb to the 1982 Pan paperback edition<br /><br />The second episode of The Saga of The Exiles takes us deeper into May’s bizarre, cruel and beautiful Pliocene civilisation. Bryan, who travelled to the past to find his lost lover, Mercy, discovers her to be the wife of Nodonn, pureblood Tanu, leader of The Host of Nontusvel (i.e. the innumerable Tanu children of the Queen and King Thagdal) and, via her golden torc, one of the most powerful Creators in the Elder Earth.<br />Bryan little realises that his sociological survey of Tanu society will throw the world into turmoil, since it shows that the effect of human interaction with the Tanu will spell their doom.<br />Meanwhile, Elizabeth meets Brede, the prescient bride of the living ship in which the Tanu and Firvulag came to Earth. She is neither Tanu nor Firvulag, but a mixture of both, coming from a separate world in the Tanu galaxy where the split between Tanu and Firvulag did not occur.<br />Madame Guderian and Claude manage to seal the Time Portal to prevent more humans coming through, but Aiken Drum betrays the rest of his fellows who plan to attack the Torc factory.<br />Felice, tortured by Culluket the Interrogator, is forced into operancy, but driven insane.<br />The time of the Great Combat approaches but it seems that even within the Tanu and Firvulag ranks there are those who are tiring of the old traditions.<br />Brede, having foreseen what is to come, rescues the rebels from their dungeon. Elizabeth was to have escaped with Sukie and and Stein in her balloon, but Brede also brings along the unconscious Felice, Elizabeth gives up her place in the balloon and remains behind.<br />Felice, awakening in the balloon, draws Stein into her plan to revenge herself and with her psychokinesis and Stein’s geology skills they crack the already weak barrier holding back the Atlantic ocean, allowing the ocean to pour into the dry basin of the Mediterranean, the basin in which the Tanu and Firvulag are gathered to celebrate the Grand Combat.<br />One of the surprises of this series is that May manages to combine the medieval with the futuristic, the comic with the cruel and tragic, the serious realism of some characters with the caricatured and grotesque, the past and the future, as if many of the themes were aspects of the original duality of the Tanu and Firvulag (whose home planet, incidentally, is called Duat)<br />It becomes clear to the reader that the Tanu and Firvulag did not escape our Earth of six million years ago, leaving the ramapithecines to evolve into humanity.<br />In an intriguing moment, Nodonn, who was criticised for taking a human wife, tells his brothers that he had Mercy’s genes examined, the result of which was that she was almost pure Tanu, leaving the readers to work out for themselves that we are the descendants of aliens who mated with their far future grandchildren.<br />It's impressive, addictive and just wonderful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7252308113528516253" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2126919795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126919795" />
    <a title="Jean Triceratops" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71556718-jean-triceratops"><img alt="Jean Triceratops" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527248695p2/71556718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126919795?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jean Triceratops" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jean Triceratops" href="/user/show/71556718-jean-triceratops">Jean Triceratops</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71556718-jean-triceratops?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126919795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10711238222553981024"><i>The Golden Torc</i> is the second book in <i>The Saga of Pliocene Exile</i> series. You might assume that means it picks up where the last book lets off.<br/><br/>It doesn’t.<br/><br/>It actually picks up, chronologically, about half-way through <i>The Many Colored Land</i>. Remember Aiken and Raimo and Elizabeth and Stein and Sukey? Now we get to learn what they were up to while Madame Guderian coached Felice et al through their cockamamie scheme. We follow this crew up until the timeline catches up to the end of book one, at which</span>
  <span id="freeText10711238222553981024" style="display:none"><i>The Golden Torc</i> is the second book in <i>The Saga of Pliocene Exile</i> series. You might assume that means it picks up where the last book lets off.<br /><br />It doesn’t.<br /><br />It actually picks up, chronologically, about half-way through <i>The Many Colored Land</i>. Remember Aiken and Raimo and Elizabeth and Stein and Sukey? Now we get to learn what they were up to while Madame Guderian coached Felice et al through their cockamamie scheme. We follow this crew up until the timeline catches up to the end of book one, at which point we go back to hopping between the two groups.<br /><br />This is where <i>The Golden Torc</i> starts to feel a little different than <i>The Many Colored Land</i>. We have some dozen or more primary characters, and at least double that number of secondary—yet still incredibly important—characters that we need to keep tabs on. To accomplish this feat, Julian May ups the speed while pushing a lot of occurrences off screen.<br /><br />It’s not a terrible way to handle it. The fact that characters continue to live their lives even when we’re not watching them helps add a sense of authenticity to the story and, well, with this epic of a story I can’t say the ramping speed of the narrative didn’t match my own intensity. My favorite types of books, though, are those I read for the sheer enjoyment of reading (as opposed to getting to the conclusion). <i>The Many Colored Land</i> fit that description, but I’m not sure I can say the same about <i>The Golden Torc</i>. Which isn’t to say it’s bad by any stretch, it’s just different.<br /><br />I'd also say that <i>The Golden Torc</i> feels much less sci-fi than it's predecessor. Despite some futuristic technology, the millieu is prehistoric and filled with, essentially, fairies. It's going to hard to give that a hard sci-fi edge.<br /><br />One concern I have that is continued from <i>The Many Colored Land</i> is her characterization—especially of (human) men. Richard’s sudden redemption in<i>The Many Colored Land</i> felt cheap. I appreciate that just because people are monsters in some aspects of their lives, it doesn’t preclude them from being loving elsewhere. But seriously, Richard was just plain nasty. It wasn’t days before he met his savior-love that he was hoping the Tanu had baseball-bat sized peckers and that they’d use them against a very unwilling Felice.<br /><br />This tradition of men behaving in, my opinion, unrealistic ways continues into <i>The Golden Torc</i>, though perhaps to a lesser degree. I don’t love it.<br /><br />Amusingly, though, I find May’s depiction of Tanu men (and women) to be exceptional. Perhaps it’s because, as exotics, she doesn’t feel confined to trying to get them ‘right’ or finding a character arc for them. They get to just exist—and I think that puts their characterization as the best in the book.<br /><br />I’d also like to say that Sugoll makes an appearance in this book, and he alone is worth the price of admission.<br /><br />[I read old fantasy and sci-fi novels written by women authors in search of forgotten gems. See more at <a href="https://www.forfemfan.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">forfemfan.com</a>]</span>
  <a data-text-id="10711238222553981024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710022905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5048255982822577829">Finished this a while back as part of my summer commitment to read more SFF. It's good for the brain. <br/><br/>Julian May really caught me by surprise--I hadn't heard of her until I read Chabon's paean to tricksters and SFF in Maps and Legends (which I also recommend). The Many-Colored Land took me a while to get into, but by the time I got a third of the way through I just devoured it and then chowed my way through Golden Torc. This book starts to weave back together the fates of Group Green, and if you</span>
  <span id="freeText5048255982822577829" style="display:none">Finished this a while back as part of my summer commitment to read more SFF. It's good for the brain. <br /><br />Julian May really caught me by surprise--I hadn't heard of her until I read Chabon's paean to tricksters and SFF in Maps and Legends (which I also recommend). The Many-Colored Land took me a while to get into, but by the time I got a third of the way through I just devoured it and then chowed my way through Golden Torc. This book starts to weave back together the fates of Group Green, and if you're even half-attentive to Irish myth, you'll enjoy the character work. A good mix of SF with the major fantasy elements, and well-plotted, even if I found myself having to work to keep track of some of the Tanu character names in a few spots. Lots of subplots to keep your eyes on, but I think May does a nice job of keeping them all grounded in the main action of the book. Also, I now sort of want a gold jumpsuit covered in pockets... <br /><br /> Friends, if you really loved me, you'd cruise used bookstores and find me the next two in the series, because our Half-Price only had this one and the first.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1287005918500043793">This is a fine bookend for the first book, bringing many of the storylines initiated in that book to rather solid and at times shocking conclusions. There's a big event in this book that is so evocative that it's been my primary memory of May's writing in the 20+ since years since I read it last. That's the kind of drama you want in a book!<br/><br/>Unfortunately, <i>The Golden Torc</i> also loses its way in the last third of the book.   <span id="freeText1287005918500043793" style="display:none">This is a fine bookend for the first book, bringing many of the storylines initiated in that book to rather solid and at times shocking conclusions. There's a big event in this book that is so evocative that it's been my primary memory of May's writing in the 20+ since years since I read it last. That's the kind of drama you want in a book!<br /><br />Unfortunately, <i>The Golden Torc</i> also loses its way in the last third of the book. There's too much focus on the antagonists, but none of it sufficiently concentrated that we really come to know the individuals as people. There are also too many long listings of names and battles in the end.<br /><br /><i>The Golden Torc</i> rediscovers its way in the last fifteen pages or so, which touch bases with all of our core characters, and promises more of the same in the next book, and that's where a lot of the excitement is too, but it's a bit of a trudge to get there.</span>

  <span id="freeText12951650604320097680" style="display:none">I've liked all the other books by Julian May that I've read, but I didn't enjoy this it all. Sooooo many mental powers.<br /><br />The overall situation described in the book is interesting, and Ms. May's vocabulary is impressive, but there's not much else to recommend. The book is stuffed with plot twists and minor characters, which I was not motivated to follow closely and distinguish among. I'm willing to give the next volume a chance and hope this one was just an aberration.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793497-amanda?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793497-amanda?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793497-amanda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5793497-amanda?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer885921067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15218088623181122259">This entry feels more fantastical than the first, although science definitely still factors in. It is richer in action and intrigue and perhaps a bit less focused on character development.<br/><br/>This is a difficult book to sum up, since so very much happens. It’s an action-packed chunkster, providing the reader with information and new settings without ever feeling like an info-dump. The medieval-like flare of the Tanu and the goblin/fairie/shapeshifter qualities of the Firvulag are stronger in this en</span>
  <span id="freeText15218088623181122259" style="display:none">This entry feels more fantastical than the first, although science definitely still factors in. It is richer in action and intrigue and perhaps a bit less focused on character development.<br /><br />This is a difficult book to sum up, since so very much happens. It’s an action-packed chunkster, providing the reader with information and new settings without ever feeling like an info-dump. The medieval-like flare of the Tanu and the goblin/fairie/shapeshifter qualities of the Firvulag are stronger in this entry, and it is delightful. Creating a medieval world of aliens on ancient Earth is probably the most brilliant part of the book, followed closely by the idea of torcs enhancing the brain’s abilities. May has created and weaved a complex, fascinating world that manages to also be easy enough to follow and understand.<br /><br />The intrigue is so complex that it is almost impossible to summarize, and yet it was easy to follow while reading it. Surprises lurk around every corner, and May is definitely not afraid to kill her darlings, following both William Faulkner’s and Stephen King’s writing advice. A lot happens in the book, the characters are tested, and enough change happens that I am excited there are still two more books, as opposed to wondering how the author could possibly tell more story. In spite of the action, sometimes the book did feel overly long, with long descriptions of vegetation and scenery far away from where most of the action was taking place.<br /><br />The book is full of characters but every single one of them manages to come across as a unique person, even the ones who are not on-screen long enough to be fully three-dimensional. The cast continues to be diverse, similarly to the first book, with a variety of races, ages, and sexual preferences represented. I was surprised by the addition of a transwoman character. She is treated with a mix of acceptance and transphobia. I think, certainly for the 1980s when this was published, it is overall a progressive presentation of her. She is a doctor who is well-respected in Tanu society. However, she also is presented as a bit crazy (not because of being trans but in addition to being trans), and it is stated by one character that she runs the fertility clinic because it is the one part of being a woman that will always be out of her grasp. I am glad at her inclusion in the story but readers should be aware that some aspects of the writing of her and how other characters interact with her could be considered problematic or triggering. I would be interested to hear a transperson’s analysis of her character.<br /><br />Overall, this entry in the series ramps up the action and more thoroughly investigates the world of the Pliocene Exile. Readers disappointed by the lack of information on the half of the group heading to the capital city in the first book will be pleased that their story is told in this one. Characters are added, including a transwoman doctor, and all continue to feel completely individual and easily decipherable, in spite of the growing cast list. The fast action pace sometimes is interrupted by lengthy descriptions of settings far away from the action, but overall the chunkster of the book moves along at a good pace and remains engaging. Recommended to fans of fantasy who want a touch of science in their stories and who are interested in the idea of medieval aliens.<br /><br />Check out my <a href="http://wp.me/pp7vL-16P" rel="nofollow noopener">full review</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15218088623181122259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer864428913842474317">If you have gotten this far, you will know what the setting is to the Saga of the Pliocene Exile. You may also be wondering what, exactly, is going on with the four characters that went to the Tanu capital of Muriah. And that is where the book picks up.<br/><br/>So, the reader finds themselves backwards in time before the rebel uprising at the end of The Many-Colored Land to catch up with Bryan, Aiken Drum, Elizabeth, and the 'Viking' Stein. Theirs is a much more politically driven story, as they maneuver</span>
  <span id="freeText864428913842474317" style="display:none">If you have gotten this far, you will know what the setting is to the Saga of the Pliocene Exile. You may also be wondering what, exactly, is going on with the four characters that went to the Tanu capital of Muriah. And that is where the book picks up.<br /><br />So, the reader finds themselves backwards in time before the rebel uprising at the end of The Many-Colored Land to catch up with Bryan, Aiken Drum, Elizabeth, and the 'Viking' Stein. Theirs is a much more politically driven story, as they maneuver the conniving of various factions that strive for dominance of the Many-Colored Land. As an anthropologist, Bryan embarks to complete a survey of human-Tanu relations that the King hopes to use to support is breeding program. Elizabeth, as the *cough* first fully meta-functional operant is key to that breeding program and a target for those who wish for a pure-blooded Tanu race. Aiken, meanwhile, decides that he is going to throw his hat into this game of throne and attempt to overthrow the King's heir and the King in the ritual Grand Combat so that he can be ruler over the Many-Colored Land... and Stein is caught up in Aiken's story.<br /><br />These characters are followed until the beginning of the Grand Truce, after which we are reunited with our other intrepid time-travelers as they prepare to carry out the final phases of their revolution to free humankind from Tanu control. <br /><br />And of course, in the end, we have the Grand Combat, which Julian May utilizes to grand effect to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[clear the board <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, as it were. <br /><br />Julian May writes political intrigue right. It is fun, suspenseful, and irritating. Most of all, it is not overdone. There is a good balance between the political plot of some of the characters and the adventure plots of our intrepid rebels. Furthermore, in what might seem to be revolutionary to modern readers, most of the story threads are wrapped up! *gasp!* Satisfactorily! *Wha-wha-whaaaat?*<br /><br />Kinda makes you wonder what the second half of the saga is going to be about.... *goes to read prologue to The Non-Born King* Well... they're boned.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13259143734616752911">Originally published on my blog <a href='http://simonsbookblog.blogspot.com/1998/08/julian-may-golden-torc-1982.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> in August 1998.<br/><br/>The second of May's Pliocene-set Saga of the Exiles series, The Golden Torc continues from where <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/378639.The_Many_Coloured_Land__Saga_of_Pliocene_Exile___1_' title='The Many-Coloured Land (Saga of Pliocene Exile, #1) by Julian May' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Many-Coloured Land</a> left off. The humans from the group focused upon in the first novel are continuing to make a large contribution to the alien society they have found themselves in. Aiken Drum is insinuating himself into the highest echelons of society; Elizabeth is trying not to let the Tanu take advantage of her newly recovered mental capacit</span>
  <span id="freeText13259143734616752911" style="display:none">Originally published on my blog <a href="http://simonsbookblog.blogspot.com/1998/08/julian-may-golden-torc-1982.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> in August 1998.<br /><br />The second of May's Pliocene-set Saga of the Exiles series, The Golden Torc continues from where <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/378639.The_Many_Coloured_Land__Saga_of_Pliocene_Exile___1_" title="The Many-Coloured Land (Saga of Pliocene Exile, #1) by Julian May" rel="nofollow noopener">The Many-Coloured Land</a> left off. The humans from the group focused upon in the first novel are continuing to make a large contribution to the alien society they have found themselves in. Aiken Drum is insinuating himself into the highest echelons of society; Elizabeth is trying not to let the Tanu take advantage of her newly recovered mental capacity; Richard is still seeking Mercy (who in fact has married one of the Tanu aristocracy); Claude and Felice are with the rebel "Low-Lifes".<br /><br />The novel builds to a climax at the annual battle between the Tanu and Firvulag; a variety of schemes involving the different members of the group are set to come to fruition at the tournament. They are all upstaged by the actions of Felice, who causes an earthquake which breaches the straits of Gibraltar and floods the Mediterranean with water from the Atlantic (the Mediterranean being a series of salt water marshes and lagoons at around this period, apparently), sweeping away the city of Muriah where the battle is taking place.<br /><br />The book is well put together, and the climax is in the best traditions of science fiction.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2567844147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11963628647310788609">As with the previous book, my memory made this seem better than it is. 2.5 stars for this one; it's a more focused book and more enjoyable for that. But Stein continues to be toxic as hell, making his wife break down and then against her will shutting off her mental powers, because she might use them to talk to people other than him. This after he screws everything up repeatedly by being unable to keep quiet about anything ever, and also by committing outrageous crimes. Somehow everyone values h</span>
  <span id="freeText11963628647310788609" style="display:none">As with the previous book, my memory made this seem better than it is. 2.5 stars for this one; it's a more focused book and more enjoyable for that. But Stein continues to be toxic as hell, making his wife break down and then against her will shutting off her mental powers, because she might use them to talk to people other than him. This after he screws everything up repeatedly by being unable to keep quiet about anything ever, and also by committing outrageous crimes. Somehow everyone values him enough to work to keep him alive, for reasons I cannot begin to fathom. Fortunately, he essentially will not reappear after the end of this book when (somehow) his wife is happy with him. Other issues that I never paid much attention to: the tidal wave at the end is too vastly improbable given the circumstances; why didn't the folks there at the end just fly away, as many of them could; how could the Tanu and the Firvulag survive their annual slaughter which in this book kills several thousand humans (the mainstay of the Tanu side) and plenty of Firvulag and some Tanu. Even recognizing that it was an exceptional year in that regard, the regular games would be full of deaths, too. The rather small numbers of population they have and the frightfully slow reproductive rate of the Tanu would eliminate the species pretty quickly, especially once you add in the Hunts taking their toll on the Firvulag by the hundreds collectively.</span>

These beasts are getting scarce with overhunting and I'll not have them wasted."<br /><br />We find out that the woman that Brian the anthropologist went to the past to find, Mercy, has married into the Tanu Noble family:<br />P.80-1:<br />" 'some humans belong in the Many-Colored Land. people like you, Rosmar, my green-eyed, gray-eyed love, who never truly fit into the world of Elder Earth. but not all members of your race who come through are willing to accept the Tanu as masters. (Alas the child whose child?) <br />" 'Ah, silly!' she exclained, pretending anger. 'the Thagdal's, of course, as the first must always be. You know about our jus primae noctis. and does it matter to you?'<br />" 'All that matters is that I love you. I'll always love you, no matter what you are.'<br />" 'and what do you think I am? She looked into his mind and the anger that blazed out now was real.'I'm not NoDonn's concubine! I'm his wife. He's taken me and no other.'<br />"And 16 Tanu women and 400 human latents of high talent before you...'I don't care, Mercy. Stop reading me! I can't help the way the thoughts come. They have nothing to do with my love for you.' "<br /><br />Raimo, the Forester, and Aiken Drum, the diminutive trickster, are popular with the ladies of the court. But Raimo is a coward when it comes time for The Great Games, the yearly event where the greatest warriors of the Firvulag, Tanu and humans match off:<br />P.333:<br />" 'open your eyes, chopper. You're shining knight has come to the rescue.'<br />"still prone, Raimo tilted up his visor. a huge black chaliko all armored in gold looked down at him, it's benign eyes peering from the openings of a gilded chamfron. It had a monocerine faceted spike of amethyst mounted on its forehead. sitting the magnificent beast was a diminutive human glowing as from a self-contained power source. he carried no weapon, no shield. but he held high a purple banner whose golden-hand blazon gave the finger to the Exile world. a black-and-violet cape rippled unstained about Aiken Drum's gold-lustre armor. he grinned as he pk-hoisted Raimo to his feet. <br />" 'there you go, chopper. Good as new and ready to raise hell! See you later!'<br />" 'Wait –' the former woodsman pleaded. But The Shining One was gone. the battle noise intensified and so did the clouds of smok and dust. It sounded as though some desperate engagement were coming right at him. <br />"he stumbled about until he recovered his sword and buckler. Avoiding the thrashing chaliko and the fearful mess that had been Grumpy, he started off in the direction opposite from the worst of the psychocreative detonations, away from the clang of glass and bronze weapons, the bellowing of thousands of human and inhuman voices that filled his ears and mind. within a few minutes he was completely disoriented. there was no clue to show him the way to the shore, no sure route to escape. <br />" 'what am I going to do?' He whimpered.<br />"Survive until sunset, something reminded him, and there would be a recess of three hours while the field was cleared of the wounded and the dead. If he could manage to hide until then--<br />"He tripped over the two decapitated Firvulag and stopped his aimless flight. there was no natural cover on the plain – so why not? Still shrouded in thick dust clouds, he flung himself down and burrowed among their dark-dripping limbs. Then he withdrew his consciousness into that inadequate little closet of refuge Aiken had taught him to use when the women drove him to the brink of madness. Unless someone beamed a thought right at him, he was safe. Almost all sensation, almost all pain ceased. Raimo Hakkinen then waited."<br /><br />This is book two of The many colored land series. In the ending of the book, Brian has died. In the area that in the future will be the Mediterranean sea, is a salt plain. This is where the great games are held every year. Felice has become mad with the power that the torc has given her. Stein and Sukie escape with her in a balloon, and Felice, urged on by Stein, blasts the natural land Dam that holds back the Atlantic ocean from the Mediterranean basin. She does this using her psychokinetic powers. when the great games are done, Aiken drum has defeated NoDonn, making him the king of the Tanu. but as soon as the great games are finished, a huge wall of water drowns most of the people on the salt plains, and this is how Brian dies.<br />Madame and Clyde marry. Madame wants to close down the time portal. She devises a method, scratching a message on amber, and waits with Claud near the time portal. But their plan is discovered, and they are killed. On the other end of the portal, two skeletons and a slice of amber with a message show up.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16516678895467006775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027571055?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michel Meijer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michel Meijer" href="/user/show/24081766-michel-meijer">Michel Meijer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027571055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14566412617608676503">Rereading this since years and it has become clear that part 1 and 2 of the Saga of the Pliocene Exile belong to the same story and could have been published in 1 part. So if you are interested in this, just read 1 and 2 after each other. Part 1 (the many colored land) describes the Exiles and the technicalities of the journey to the past, while part 2 gives more background on the aliens, their habits and the symbiosys between Men and Tanu/Firvulag. There is no need to give an synopsis with a fa</span>
  <span id="freeText14566412617608676503" style="display:none">Rereading this since years and it has become clear that part 1 and 2 of the Saga of the Pliocene Exile belong to the same story and could have been published in 1 part. So if you are interested in this, just read 1 and 2 after each other. Part 1 (the many colored land) describes the Exiles and the technicalities of the journey to the past, while part 2 gives more background on the aliens, their habits and the symbiosys between Men and Tanu/Firvulag. There is no need to give an synopsis with a fanatasy hero like this one. Many story lines take place in parallel and it is just waiting for the big clash to happen that seals the deal of the 2 books. Basically you expect something big as a result of the disturbance in the balance the Exiles brought with them. In book 1 the raid of Finiah is just foreplay, in the concluding Chapters of book 2 the real deal happens.<br /><br />I just love this series. The story is origional, the subplot and politics nicely interwoven with fantasy magic and personal development. All on a canvas of great descriptions of the Pliocenic European world. I think the first book is better than the second, but it is very close. 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14566412617608676503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1857024036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4070432083263536342">As with the first book in the Saga of Exiles series, this—the second—is remarkable for its meticulous and absorbing world-building. I did feel, however, that all the detail rather obscured the plot, which was slow to unfold and not sufficiently signposted. Often, I found myself enjoying the scenery without knowing where I was going. There are a lot of characters—a LOT—which made it difficult to remember who was who and tough to feel any sense of engagement. These quibbles aside, THE GOLDEN TORC </span>
  <span id="freeText4070432083263536342" style="display:none">As with the first book in the Saga of Exiles series, this—the second—is remarkable for its meticulous and absorbing world-building. I did feel, however, that all the detail rather obscured the plot, which was slow to unfold and not sufficiently signposted. Often, I found myself enjoying the scenery without knowing where I was going. There are a lot of characters—a LOT—which made it difficult to remember who was who and tough to feel any sense of engagement. These quibbles aside, THE GOLDEN TORC does come together in the final quarter and the pay off is worth it. Definitely, I enjoyed it more than THE MANY COLOURED LAND (which I also enjoyed) and am sufficiently hooked to continue on to the third book, THE NON BORN KING.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3198333630313531696">In general I give all series two volumes to entice me to read further—in this case, May has failed utterly. Somehow she has taken a good concept and serviceable storytelling and written a book almost entirely devoid of interest. The few sympathetic characters she presents have so minor a role that finding out what happens to them has next to no appeal. I've watched all people and events become slowly more sterile and cold, and in the end I had to push myself to read the last hundred pages. I'm l</span>
  <span id="freeText3198333630313531696" style="display:none">In general I give all series two volumes to entice me to read further—in this case, May has failed utterly. Somehow she has taken a good concept and serviceable storytelling and written a book almost entirely devoid of interest. The few sympathetic characters she presents have so minor a role that finding out what happens to them has next to no appeal. I've watched all people and events become slowly more sterile and cold, and in the end I had to push myself to read the last hundred pages. I'm left with absolutely no desire to finish the series—it's a waste of time. I should have gone with my instinct after finishing the first book.</span>

<div id="review_2988126845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2988126845" />
    <a title="Betawolf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69041363-betawolf"><img alt="Betawolf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528362974p2/69041363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2988126845?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betawolf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betawolf" href="/user/show/69041363-betawolf">Betawolf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330267199" href="/book/show/1018534.The_Golden_Torc">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69041363-betawolf?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69041363-betawolf?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2988126845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2151405063257405530">I guess for consistency's sake I shall continue labeling this science-fiction, although really you could make an argument that it is more like a fantasy epic with a veneer of scifi. Some of the paleobiology seems to slip, and while there aren't quite dinosaurs wandering around, there are some distant relatives out of archeological place. Most of the book is caught up in the internal intrigue and the action of the major power-players (Aiken, Felice, Elizabeth and the big Tanu figures), which feel</span>
  <span id="freeText2151405063257405530" style="display:none">I guess for consistency's sake I shall continue labeling this science-fiction, although really you could make an argument that it is more like a fantasy epic with a veneer of scifi. Some of the paleobiology seems to slip, and while there aren't quite dinosaurs wandering around, there are some distant relatives out of archeological place. Most of the book is caught up in the internal intrigue and the action of the major power-players (Aiken, Felice, Elizabeth and the big Tanu figures), which feels quite appropriate and has enough reversals and twists that it's entertaining. <br /><br />There is an appropriately climactic finish, handling both the character development and the broader picture quite well. The pageantry of the Grand Combat pairs well with Felice and Stein's crushing revenge. I wasn't overall that impressed by anything, but it's a decent enough read. I am somewhat puzzled as to how May will continue from here, though -- while only Claude has technically died of the original eight, several of the others seem to have played their part. I'm still interested enough to keep reading and find out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2151405063257405530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/ghu4wL/IVKF+2I/fSYwg70o7UzcX8QwJpFUdlcEEJSI7LIsGBTCukPeOfFw6rzGccPf/CZEMqthiUmn7PdBlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XF+G1dHK8jo0f+nKFFG6KJcLRuuc+Y4++38UfZopvucqu1oayyER0vJasgQZnTZtW+B0W2bieKW8ZwmsIdrv5g==')})
  }
